< review>
I just needed a presta to schrader adapter which I bought for $2.15 (most shops have them for $1.00) then I needed to use the compressor to attempt to see if a tubeless conversion wheel I am building would hold air or if I need more rim tape so the tire will seat properly with the conversion strip. The guy said he couldn't just let me use it but he could do it though he would have to charge me even though I had just made a purchase. He seemed awfully put out and more interested in money than in helping a cyclist. when I explained what I was doing and dared to ask if he knew about tubeless, he pompously said "I know all about it" as if offended. He reluctantly made an attempt to put air in and when it wouldn't work he just said "there is something fundamentally wrong" without offering any solution (which I didn't actually need). I have worked in many bike shops and was looking for a good, helpful one locally. I won't be going back.< /review>

Three Pickles on Canon Perdido has so many things going for it besides having the best sandwiches in town. First of all, it has some of the best views in Santa Barbara when you sit in the patio/alley. It's next to the best coffee shop in town, Handlebar. And best of all, the Pickles bar (located in a historic building that once housed an opium den and brothel) has an all star team of bartenders all with different specialties. I find myself there for breakfast, lunch and dinner for drinks! It's a real gem.< /text>

<user_name>Zach< /user_name><Date>1610147066600</Date>< rating>
5<//rating>
< review>
This place was a total surprise find for my friends and I. They where visiting from Arizona (small town) and don't have any puzzle shops, but love to solve them so we stopped by right when they opened up. The guy (don't know his name, but he has a funny name tag that just says"I work here") he made our experience amazingly fun. Yes, the shop follows COVID protocols so the moment you go in you are prompted to immediately use hand sanitizer before you start to solve the puzzles on the podiums. Before we knew it with the jokes and portal references (the clerk was give glados inspired encouragement, that was a roasting and yet extremely hilarious) we got stuck in this shop for an 1hr and 30 minutes just solving puzzles and having laughs with the clerk. This place was lots of fun and definitely worth a visit if you like puzzles to solve and have plenty of time to kill.<//review>

< text>
My go-to sushi place. The store is extremely small and intimate. The staff know you by name. The proprietor is warm and very chatty. She always gives me special dishes or extra sake on the house because I've been dining there for years. The food is excellent and usually arrives very quickly. <user_id>107098871506549829751</user_id>< username>
Stanley Fletcher<//username>
<date>1478020572164<//date><rating>5< /rating>< text>
Don't be fooled by the size of this establishment, the portions are anything but small. The salmon sashimi, for example, is about 8+ pieces cut thick, about 3/4 inch thick. The rolls are huge as well.

I typically power through 3-5 rolls and several orders of sashimi at other local establishments. At Goleta sushi house I struggle to get past 2-3 rolls and one order of sashimi.

The fish quality is also on par with other local sushi joints, I have found it to be slightly better and more consistently fresh than other places.

The owner is a delightfully attentive lady and the staff she keeps are helpful to the best of their abilities. Sometimes there is a language barrier with some of them, but they are always courteous and accommodating.< /text>
